             <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">

           <th style="padding-right:1em">
            Result
           </th>
           <td>
            <p>
             American victory
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">
               Treaty of Paris
              </a>
              of 1898
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th style="padding-right:1em">
            Territorial
            <br/>
            changes
           </th>
           <td>
            Spain relinquishes sovereignty over Cuba, cedes
            <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
             Puerto Rico
            </a>
            ,
            <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
             Guam
            </a>
            and the
            <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
             Philippine Islands
            </a>
            to the United States for $20 million
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </td>

       <tr>
        <td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">
         <span class="flagicon">

         </span>

          </a>

         </span>
         53,000 rebels

          <a href="#cite_note-5">
           [c]
          </a>
         </sup>

         </span>
         40,000 rebels

         </sup>

       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">
         Casualties and losses
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">
         <p>
          <b>
           American:
          </b>
         </p>
         <ul>
          <li>
           281 killed and 1,577 wounded
           <small>
            (Army)
           </small>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeenan200170_9-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeenan200170-9">
             [5]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           16 killed and 68 wounded
           <small>
            (Navy)
           </small>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeenan200170_9-1">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeenan200170-9">
             [5]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           2,061 dead from disease
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255_10-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255-10">
             [6]
            </a>
           </sup>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
            <a href="#cite_note-11">
             [7]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           11 prisoners
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
            <a href="#cite_note-12">
             [8]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           1 cargo ship sunk
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
            <a href="#cite_note-13">
             [9]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           1 cruiser damaged
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255_10-1">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255-10">
             [6]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td style="width:50%;padding-left:0.25em">
         <p>
          <b>
           Spanish:
          </b>
         </p>
         <ul>
          <li>
           200 killed and 400 wounded
           <small>
            (Army)
           </small>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeenan200170_9-2">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeenan200170-9">
             [5]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           500–600 killed and 300–400 wounded
           <small>
            (Navy)
           </small>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeenan200170_9-3">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeenan200170-9">
             [5]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           15,000 dead from disease
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETucker2009[https://books.google.com.ph/books?id=8V3vZxOmHssC&amp;pg=PA105#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false_105]_14-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETucker2009[https://books.google.com.ph/books?id=8V3vZxOmHssC&amp;pg=PA105#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false_105]-14">
             [10]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           40,000+ prisoners
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255_10-2">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255-10">
             [6]
            </a>
           </sup>
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
            <a href="#cite_note-15">
             [11]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           6 small ships sunk
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255_10-3">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255-10">
             [6]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           11 cruisers sunk
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255_10-4">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255-10">
             [6]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           2 destroyers sunk
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255_10-5">
            <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017255-10">
             [6]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="font-size:90%;border-top:1px solid #aaa;">
         <p>
          The higher naval losses may be attributed to the disastrous naval defeats inflicted on the Spanish at
          <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_Bay" title="Battle of Manila Bay">
           Manila Bay
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Battle of Santiago de Cuba">
           Santiago de Cuba
          </a>
          .

         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cuba.svg">
          <img alt="Flag of Cuba.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="800" height="8" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/16px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/24px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/32px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png 2x" width="16"/>

       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">
         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
          <ul>
           <li class="nv-view">
            <a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Cuba" title="Template:History of Cuba">
             <abbr title="View this template">
              v
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-talk">
            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Cuba" title="Template talk:History of Cuba">
             <abbr title="Discuss this template">
              t
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-edit">
            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Cuba&amp;action=edit">
             <abbr title="Edit this template">
              e
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Spanish–American War
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         Guerra hispano-americana
        </span>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         Guerra hispano-estadounidense
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">
        Filipino
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="fil" xml:lang="fil">
         Digmaang Espanyol-Amerikano
        </span>
       </i>
       ) was fought between the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spain_under_the_Restoration" title="Spain under the Restoration">
        Spain
       </a>
       in 1898. Hostilities began in the aftermath of the internal explosion of the
       <a href="/wiki/USS_Maine_(ACR-1)" title="USS Maine (ACR-1)">
        USS
        <i>
         Maine
        </i>
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Havana_Harbor" title="Havana Harbor">
        Havana Harbor
       </a>
       in Cuba, leading to U.S. intervention in the
       <a href="/wiki/Cuban_War_of_Independence" title="Cuban War of Independence">
        Cuban War of Independence
       </a>
       . American acquisition of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">
        Spain's Pacific possessions
       </a>
       led to its involvement in the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">
        Philippine Revolution
       </a>
       and ultimately in the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">
        Philippine–American War
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The main issue was Cuban independence. Revolts had been occurring for some years in Cuba against Spanish rule. The U.S. later backed these revolts upon entering the Spanish–American War. There had been war scares before, as in the
       <a href="/wiki/Virginius_Affair" title="Virginius Affair">
        Virginius Affair
       </a>
       in 1873, but in the late 1890s, U.S. public opinion was agitated by anti-Spanish propaganda led by newspaper publishers such as
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Pulitzer" title="Joseph Pulitzer">
        Joseph Pulitzer
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/William_Randolph_Hearst" title="William Randolph Hearst">
        William Randolph Hearst
       </a>
       which used
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_journalism" title="Yellow journalism">
        yellow journalism
       </a>
       to call for war.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The business community across the United States had just recovered from a deep depression and feared that a war would reverse the gains. It lobbied vigorously against going to war.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">
        United States Navy
       </a>
       armoured cruiser
       <a href="/wiki/USS_Maine_(ACR-1)" title="USS Maine (ACR-1)">
        <i>
         Maine
        </i>
       </a>
       had mysteriously sunk in
       <a href="/wiki/Havana_Harbor" title="Havana Harbor">
        Havana Harbor
       </a>
       ; political pressures from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="History of the Democratic Party (United States)">
        Democratic Party
       </a>
       pushed the administration of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="History of the Republican Party (United States)">
        Republican
       </a>
       President
       <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">
        William McKinley
       </a>
       into a war that he had wished to avoid.
      </p>
      <p>
       President McKinley signed a joint Congressional resolution demanding Spanish withdrawal and authorizing the President to use military force to help Cuba gain independence on April 20, 1898.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stat33.738_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-stat33.738-20">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In response, Spain severed diplomatic relations with the United States on April 21. On the same day, the U.S. Navy began a
       <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">
        blockade
       </a>
       of Cuba.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trask57_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-trask57-21">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On April 23, Spain stated that it would declare war if the U.S. forces invaded its territory. On April 25, Congress declared that a state of war between the U.S. and Spain had de facto existed since April 21, the day the blockade of Cuba had begun.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The United States sent an ultimatum to Spain demanding that it surrender control of Cuba, but due to Spain not replying soon enough, the United States had assumed Spain had ignored the ultimatum and continued to occupy Cuba.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
          <span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2017)">
           not in citation given
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The ten-week war was fought in both the Caribbean and the Pacific. As the American agitators for war well knew,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-24">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       U.S. naval power proved decisive, allowing expeditionary forces to disembark in Cuba against a Spanish garrison already facing nationwide Cuban insurgent attacks and further wasted by
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">
        yellow fever
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       American, Cuban, and Philippine forces obtained the surrender of
       <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">
        Santiago de Cuba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
        Manila
       </a>
       despite the good performance of some Spanish infantry units and fierce fighting for positions such as
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Juan_Hill" title="Battle of San Juan Hill">
        San Juan Hill
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Madrid
       <a href="/wiki/Suing_for_peace" title="Suing for peace">
        sued for peace
       </a>
       after two obsolete Spanish squadrons sunk in
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Battle of Santiago de Cuba">
        Santiago de Cuba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_Bay" title="Battle of Manila Bay">
        Manila Bay
       </a>
       and a third, more modern fleet was recalled home to protect the Spanish coasts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108–109_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-108–109-27">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The result was the 1898
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">
        Treaty of Paris
       </a>
       , negotiated on terms favorable to the U.S. which allowed it temporary
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Government_in_Cuba" title="United States Military Government in Cuba">
        control of Cuba
       </a>
       and ceded ownership of
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Insular_Government_of_the_Philippine_Islands" title="Insular Government of the Philippine Islands">
        the Philippine islands
       </a>
       . The cession of the Philippines involved payment of $20 million ($588,320,000 today) to Spain by the U.S. to cover infrastructure owned by Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The defeat and loss of the last remnants of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       was a profound shock to Spain's national psyche and provoked a thorough philosophical and artistic revaluation of Spanish society known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Generation_of_%2798" title="Generation of '98">
        Generation of '98
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108–109_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-108–109-27">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The United States gained several island possessions spanning the globe and a rancorous new debate over the wisdom of
       <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">
        expansionism
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was one of only five US wars (against a total of eleven sovereign states) to have been
       <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_war_by_the_United_States" title="Declaration of war by the United States">
        formally declared
       </a>
       by the U.S. Congress.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_background">
        Historical background
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span id="Spain.27s_attitude_towards_its_colonies">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spain's_attitude_towards_its_colonies">
        Spain's attitude towards its colonies
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The combined problems arising from the
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">
        Peninsular War
       </a>
       (1807–1814), the loss of most of its
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        colonies in the Americas
       </a>
       in the early 19th-century
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">
        Spanish American wars of independence
       </a>
       , and three
       <a href="/wiki/Carlist_Wars" title="Carlist Wars">
        Carlist Wars
       </a>
       (1832–1876) marked the low point of Spanish colonialism.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Liberal Spanish elites like
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_C%C3%A1novas_del_Castillo" title="Antonio Cánovas del Castillo">
        Antonio Cánovas del Castillo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Castelar" title="Emilio Castelar">
        Emilio Castelar
       </a>
       offered new interpretations of the concept of "empire" to dovetail with Spain's emerging nationalism. Cánovas made clear in an address to the
       <a href="/wiki/Complutense_University_of_Madrid" title="Complutense University of Madrid">
        University of Madrid
       </a>
       in 1882
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       his view of the Spanish nation as based on shared cultural and linguistic elements – on both sides of the Atlantic – that tied Spain's territories together.
      </p>
      <p>
       Cánovas saw Spanish imperialism as markedly different in its methods and purposes of colonization from those of rival empires like the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">
        French
       </a>
       . Spaniards regarded the spreading of
       <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">
        civilization
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       as Spain's major objective and contribution to the
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The concept of cultural unity bestowed special significance on Cuba, which had been Spanish for almost four hundred years, and was viewed as an integral part of the Spanish nation. The focus on preserving the empire would have negative consequences for Spain's national pride in the aftermath of the Spanish–American War.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="American_interest_in_the_Caribbean">
        American interest in the Caribbean
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1823, American fifth President
       <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">
        James Monroe
       </a>
       (1758-1831, served 1817-1825) enunciated the
       <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">
        Monroe Doctrine
       </a>
       , which stated that the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       would not tolerate further efforts by
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        European
       </a>
       governments to retake, expand their colonial holdings in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       or to interfere with the newly independent states in the hemisphere; at the same time, the doctrine stated that the U.S. would respect the status of the existing European colonies. Before the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
        American Civil War
       </a>
       (1861-1865), Southern interests attempted to have the United States purchase
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       and convert it into a new slave territory. The
       <a href="/wiki/Ostend_Manifesto" title="Ostend Manifesto">
        Ostend Manifesto
       </a>
       proposal of 1854 failed, and national attention shifted to the growing sectional conflict and threat of civil war.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the American Civil War and Cuba's
       <a href="/wiki/Ten_Years%27_War" title="Ten Years' War">
        Ten Years' War
       </a>
       , U.S. businessmen began monopolizing the devalued sugar markets in Cuba. In 1894, 90% of Cuba's total exports went to the United States, which also provided 40% of Cuba's imports.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cuba's total exports to the U.S. were almost twelve times larger than the export to her mother country,
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       U.S. business interests indicated that while Spain still held political authority over Cuba, economic authority in Cuba, acting-authority, was shifting to the U.S.A.
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. became interested in a trans-isthmus canal across
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central America
       </a>
       , either in
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       , or in
       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">
        Panama
       </a>
       , where the
       <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">
        Panama Canal
       </a>
       would later be built (1903–1914), and realized the need for naval protection. Captain
       <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Thayer_Mahan" title="Alfred Thayer Mahan">
        Alfred Thayer Mahan
       </a>
       was an especially influential theorist; his ideas were much admired by future 26th President
       <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">
        Theodore Roosevelt
       </a>
       , as the U.S. rapidly built a powerful
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">
        naval fleet
       </a>
       of steel warships in the 1880s and 1890s. Roosevelt served as
       <a href="/wiki/Assistant_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="Assistant Secretary of the Navy">
        Assistant Secretary of the Navy
       </a>
       in 1897–1898 and was an aggressive supporter of a war with Spain]] over Cuba.
      </p>
      <p>
       Meanwhile, the "Cuba Libre" movement, led by Cuban intellectual
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%AD" title="José Martí">
        José Martí
       </a>
       , had established offices in
       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">
        Florida
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">
        New York
       </a>
       to buy and smuggle weapons. It mounted a large propaganda campaign to generate sympathy that would lead to official pressure on Spain.
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestant
       </a>
       churches and
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
        Democratic
       </a>
       farmers were supportive, but business interests called on
       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">
        Washington
       </a>
       to ignore them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although Cuba attracted American attention, little note was made of the Philippines, Guam, or Puerto Rico.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Historians note that there was little popular demand in the United States for an overseas colonial empire, though at this time the longtime colonial empires of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Northern_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">
        Great Britain
       </a>
       ) with its
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British Empire
       </a>
       "on which the sun never set" and
       <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">
        France's
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">
        French Empire
       </a>
       maintained theirs with some added growths and additions, now joined by the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        German Empire
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_Empire" title="Italian Empire">
        Italian Empire
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">
        Empire of Japan
       </a>
       . These new and growing empires were dramatically expanding their overseas holdings during the late 19th century in unclaimed areas among native and indigenous peoples in the less developed continents of
       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">
        Asia
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Path_to_war">
        Path to war
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuban_struggle_for_independence">
        Cuban struggle for independence
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Cuban_War_of_Independence" title="Cuban War of Independence">
        Cuban War of Independence
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first serious bid for Cuban independence, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ten_Years%27_War" title="Ten Years' War">
        Ten Years' War
       </a>
       , erupted in 1868 and was subdued by the authorities a decade later. Neither the fighting nor the reforms in the
       <a href="/wiki/Pact_of_Zanj%C3%B3n" title="Pact of Zanjón">
        Pact of Zanjón
       </a>
       (February 1878) quelled the desire of some revolutionaries for wider autonomy and ultimately independence. One such revolutionary,
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%AD" title="José Martí">
        José Martí
       </a>
       , continued to promote Cuban financial and political autonomy in exile. In early 1895, after years of organizing, Martí launched a three-pronged invasion of the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-41">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The plan called for one group from
       <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">
        Santo Domingo
       </a>
       led by
       <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1ximo_G%C3%B3mez" title="Máximo Gómez">
        Máximo Gómez
       </a>
       , one group from
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">
        Costa Rica
       </a>
       led by
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Maceo_Grajales" title="Antonio Maceo Grajales">
        Antonio Maceo Grajales
       </a>
       , and another from the United States (preemptively thwarted by U.S. officials in Florida) to land in different places on the island and provoke an uprising. While their call for revolution, the
       <i>
        grito de Baíre
       </i>
       , was successful, the result was not the grand show of force Martí had expected. With a quick victory effectively lost, the revolutionaries settled in to fight a protracted guerrilla campaign.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_41-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-41">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Antonio Cánovas del Castillo, the architect of Spain's Restoration constitution and the prime minister at the time, ordered General
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arsenio_Mart%C3%ADnez-Campos_y_Ant%C3%B3n" title="Arsenio Martínez-Campos y Antón">
        Arsenio Martínez-Campos
       </a>
       , a distinguished veteran of the war against the previous uprising in Cuba, to quell the revolt. Campos's reluctance to accept his new assignment and his method of containing the revolt to the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Oriente_Province" title="Oriente Province">
        Oriente
       </a>
       earned him criticism in the Spanish press.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-online_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-online-42">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The mounting pressure forced Cánovas to replace General Campos with General
       <a href="/wiki/Valeriano_Weyler" title="Valeriano Weyler">
        Valeriano Weyler
       </a>
       , a soldier who had experience in quelling rebellions in overseas provinces and the Spanish metropole. Weyler deprived the insurgency of weaponry, supplies, and assistance by ordering the residents of some Cuban districts to move to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" title="Concentration camp">
        reconcentration areas
       </a>
       near the military headquarters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-online_42-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-online-42">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This strategy was effective in slowing the spread of rebellion. In the United States, this fueled the fire of anti-Spanish propaganda.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In a political speech President
       <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">
        William McKinley
       </a>
       used this to ram Spanish actions against armed rebels. He even said this "was not civilized warfare" but "extermination".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_attitude">
        Spanish attitude
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_fallera_de_l%27oncle_Sam.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1134" data-file-width="1324" height="317" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/La_fallera_de_l%27oncle_Sam.JPG/370px-La_fallera_de_l%27oncle_Sam.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/La_fallera_de_l%27oncle_Sam.JPG/555px-La_fallera_de_l%27oncle_Sam.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/La_fallera_de_l%27oncle_Sam.JPG/740px-La_fallera_de_l%27oncle_Sam.JPG 2x" width="370"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_fallera_de_l%27oncle_Sam.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">
          Spanish
         </a>
         satirical drawing published in
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/La_Campana_de_Gr%C3%A0cia" title="La Campana de Gràcia">
           La Campana de Gràcia
          </a>
         </i>
         (1896) criticizing U.S. behavior regarding Cuba by
         <a class="extiw" href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Molin%C3%A9_i_Muns" title="ca:Manuel Moliné i Muns">
          Manuel Moliné
         </a>
         . Upper text reads (in old
         <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
          Catalan
         </a>
         ): "Uncle Sam's craving", and below: "To keep the island so it won't get lost."
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Judge-2-6-1897.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="700" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Judge-2-6-1897.jpg/370px-Judge-2-6-1897.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Judge-2-6-1897.jpg/555px-Judge-2-6-1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/Judge-2-6-1897.jpg 2x" width="370"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Judge-2-6-1897.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An American cartoon published in
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Judge_(magazine)" title="Judge (magazine)">
           Judge
          </a>
         </i>
         , Feb. 6, 1897:
         <a href="/wiki/Columbia_(name)" title="Columbia (name)">
          Columbia
         </a>
         (representing the American people) reaches out to the oppressed Cuba (the caption under the chained child reads "Spain's 16th Century methods") while
         <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Sam" title="Uncle Sam">
          Uncle Sam
         </a>
         (representing the US government) sits blindfolded, refusing to see the atrocities or use his guns to intervene (cartoon by
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Grant_E._Hamilton&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Grant E. Hamilton (page does not exist)">
          Grant E. Hamilton
         </a>
         ).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Spanish Government regarded Cuba as a province of Spain rather than a colony, and depended on it for prestige and trade, and as a training ground for the army.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Prime_Minister" title="Spanish Prime Minister">
        Spanish Prime Minister
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_C%C3%A1novas_del_Castillo" title="Antonio Cánovas del Castillo">
        Antonio Cánovas del Castillo
       </a>
       announced that "the Spanish nation is disposed to sacrifice to the last peseta of its treasure and to the last drop of blood of the last Spaniard before consenting that anyone snatch from it even one piece of its territory."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He had long dominated and stabilized Spanish politics. He was assassinated in 1897 by Italian anarchist
       <a href="/wiki/Michele_Angiolillo" title="Michele Angiolillo">
        Michele Angiolillo
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       leaving a Spanish political system that was not stable and could not risk a blow to its prestige.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._response">
        U.S. response
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_William_McKinley" title="Presidency of William McKinley">
        Presidency of William McKinley
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The eruption of the Cuban revolt, Weyler's measures, and the popular fury these events whipped up proved to be a boon to the newspaper industry in New York City, where
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Pulitzer" title="Joseph Pulitzer">
        Joseph Pulitzer
       </a>
       of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_World" title="New York World">
         New York World
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/William_Randolph_Hearst" title="William Randolph Hearst">
        William Randolph Hearst
       </a>
       of the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Journal" title="New York Journal">
         New York Journal
        </a>
       </i>
       recognized the potential for great headlines and stories that would sell copies. Both papers denounced Spain, but had little influence outside New York. American opinion generally saw Spain as a hopelessly backward power that was unable to deal fairly with Cuba. American Catholics were divided before the war began, but supported it enthusiastically once it started.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. had important economic interests that were being harmed by the prolonged conflict and deepening uncertainty about the future of Cuba. Shipping firms that had relied heavily on trade with Cuba now suffered losses as the conflict continued unresolved.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These firms pressed Congress and McKinley to seek an end to the revolt. Other American business concerns, specifically those who had invested in Cuban sugar, looked to the Spanish to restore order.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Stability, not war, was the goal of both interests. How stability would be achieved would depend largely on the ability of Spain and the U.S. to work out their issues diplomatically.
      </p>
      <p>
       While tension increased among the Cubans and Spanish Government, popular support of intervention began to spring up in the United States, due to the emergence of the "Cuba Libre" movement and the fact that many Americans had drawn parallels between the American Revolution and the Cuban revolt, seeing the Spanish Government as the tyrannical colonial oppressor. Historian Louis Pérez notes that "The proposition of war in behalf of Cuban independence took hold immediately and held on thereafter. Such was the sense of the public mood." At the time many poems and songs were written in the United States to express support of the "Cuba Libre" movement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the same time, many
       <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">
        African Americans
       </a>
       , facing growing racial discrimination and increasing retardation of their civil rights, wanted to take part in the war because they saw it as a way to advance the cause of equality, service to country hopefully helping to gain political and public respect amongst the wider population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       President McKinley, well aware of the political complexity surrounding the conflict, wanted to end the revolt peacefully. In accordance with this policy, McKinley began to negotiate with the Spanish government, hoping that the negotiations would be able to end the yellow journalism in the United States, and therefore, end the loudest calls to go to war with Spain. An attempt was made to negotiate a peace before McKinley took office, however, the Spanish refused to take part in the negotiations. In 1897 McKinley appointed
       <a href="/wiki/Stewart_L._Woodford" title="Stewart L. Woodford">
        Stewart L. Woodford
       </a>
       as the new minister to Spain, who again offered to negotiate a peace. In October 1897, the Spanish government still refused the United States offer to negotiate between the Spanish and the Cubans, but promised the U.S. it would give the Cubans more autonomy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-55">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, with the election of a more liberal Spanish government in November, Spain began to change their policies in Cuba. First, the new Spanish government told the United States that it was willing to offer a change in the Reconcentration policies (the main set of policies that was feeding yellow journalism in the United States) if the Cuban rebels agreed to a cessation of hostilities. This time the rebels refused the terms in hopes that continued conflict would lead to U.S. intervention and the creation of an independent Cuba.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_55-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-55">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The liberal Spanish government also recalled the Spanish Governor General Valeriano Weyler from Cuba. This action alarmed many Cubans loyal to Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-56">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Cubans loyal to Weyler began planning large demonstrations to take place when the next Governor General, Ramon Blanco, arrived in Cuba. U.S. consul Fitzhugh Lee learned of these plans and sent a request to the U.S. State Department to send a U.S. warship to Cuba.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_56-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-56">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This request lead to the U.S.S.
       <i>
        Maine
       </i>
       being sent to Cuba. While the
       <i>
        Maine
       </i>
       was docked in Havana, an explosion sank the ship. The sinking of the
       <i>
        Maine
       </i>
       was blamed on the Spanish and made the possibility of a negotiated peace very slim.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Throughout the negotiation process, the major European powers, especially Britain, France, and Russia, generally supported the American position and urged Spain to give in.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spain repeatedly promised specific reforms that would pacify Cuba but failed to deliver; American patience ran out.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="USS_Maine_dispatch_to_Havana_and_loss">
        USS
        <i>
         Maine
        </i>
        dispatch to Havana and loss
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/USS_Maine_(ACR-1)" title="USS Maine (ACR-1)">
        USS Maine (ACR-1)
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USSMaine.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="315" data-file-width="400" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/USSMaine.jpg/250px-USSMaine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/USSMaine.jpg/375px-USSMaine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/USSMaine.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USSMaine.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The sunken
         <a href="/wiki/USS_Maine_(ACR-1)" title="USS Maine (ACR-1)">
          USS
          <i>
           Maine
          </i>
         </a>
         in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Havana_harbor" title="Havana harbor">
          Havana harbor
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       McKinley sent the USS
       <i>
        Maine
       </i>
       to Havana to ensure the safety of American citizens and interests, and to underscore the urgent need for reform. Naval forces were moved in position to attack simultaneously on several fronts if the war was not avoided. As
       <i>
        Maine
       </i>
       left Florida, a large part of the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Squadron" title="North Atlantic Squadron">
        North Atlantic Squadron
       </a>
       was moved to Key West and the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">
        Gulf of Mexico
       </a>
       . Others were also moved just off the shore of Lisbon, and still others were moved to Hong Kong.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-offner2004p56_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-offner2004p56-60">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At 9:40 on the evening of February 15, 1898,
       <i>
        Maine
       </i>
       sank in
       <a href="/wiki/Havana_Harbor" title="Havana Harbor">
        Havana Harbor
       </a>
       after suffering a massive explosion. While McKinley urged patience and did not declare that Spain had caused the explosion, the deaths of 250 out of 355
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       sailors on board focused American attention. McKinley asked Congress to appropriate $50 million for defense, and Congress unanimously obliged. Most American leaders took the position that the cause of the explosion was unknown, but public attention was now riveted on the situation and Spain could not find a diplomatic solution to avoid war. Spain appealed to the European powers, most of whom advised it to accept U.S. conditions for Cuba in order to avoid war.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Germany urged a united European stand against the United States but took no action.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETucker2009[https://books.google.com/books?id=8V3vZxOmHssC&amp;pg=PA614_614]_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETucker2009[https://books.google.com/books?id=8V3vZxOmHssC&amp;pg=PA614_614]-63">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. Navy's investigation, made public on March 28, concluded that the ship's powder magazines were ignited when an external explosion was set off under the ship's hull. This report poured fuel on popular indignation in the U.S., making the war inevitable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-offner2004p57_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-offner2004p57-64">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spain's investigation came to the opposite conclusion: the explosion originated within the ship. Other investigations in later years came to various contradictory conclusions, but had no bearing on the coming of the war. In 1974, Admiral
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyman_George_Rickover" title="Hyman George Rickover">
        Hyman George Rickover
       </a>
       had his staff look at the documents and decided there was an internal explosion. A study commissioned by
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)">
         National Geographic
        </a>
       </i>
       magazine in 1999, using AME computer modelling, stated that the explosion could have been caused by a mine, but no definitive evidence was found.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Declaring_war">
        Declaring war
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Propaganda_of_the_Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Propaganda of the Spanish–American War">
        Propaganda of the Spanish–American War
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_A_Wikoff.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="163" data-file-width="120" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/4e/Charles_A_Wikoff.jpg" width="120"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_A_Wikoff.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         United States Army Colonel
         <a href="/wiki/Charles_A._Wikoff" title="Charles A. Wikoff">
          Charles A. Wikoff
         </a>
         was the most senior U.S. military officer killed in the Spanish–American War.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the
       <i>
        Maine
       </i>
       was destroyed, New York City newspaper publishers Hearst and Pulitzer decided that the Spanish were to blame, and they publicized this theory as fact in their papers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They both used sensationalistic and astonishing accounts of "atrocities" committed by the Spanish in Cuba by using headlines in their newspapers, such as "Spanish Murderers" and "Remember The Maine". Their press exaggerated what was happening and how the Spanish were treating the Cuban prisoners.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The stories were based on factual accounts, but most of the time, the articles that were published were embellished and written with incendiary language causing emotional and often heated responses among readers. A common myth falsely states that when illustrator
       <a href="/wiki/Frederic_Remington" title="Frederic Remington">
        Frederic Remington
       </a>
       said there was no war brewing in Cuba, Hearst responded: "You furnish the pictures and I'll furnish the war."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This new "
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_journalism" title="Yellow journalism">
        yellow journalism
       </a>
       " was, however, uncommon outside New York City, and historians no longer consider it the major force shaping the national mood.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Public opinion nationwide did demand immediate action, overwhelming the efforts of President McKinley,
       <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">
        Speaker of the House
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Brackett_Reed" title="Thomas Brackett Reed">
        Thomas Brackett Reed
       </a>
       , and the business community to find a negotiated solution. Wall Street, big business, high finance and Main Street businesses across the country were vocally opposed to war and demanded peace. After years of severe depression, the economic outlook for the domestic economy was suddenly bright again in 1897. However, the uncertainties of warfare posed a serious threat to full economic recovery. "War would impede the march of prosperity and put the country back many years," warned the
       <i>
        New Jersey Trade Review.
       </i>
       The leading railroad magazine editorialized, "From a commercial and mercenary standpoint it seems peculiarly bitter that this war should come when the country had already suffered so much and so needed rest and peace." McKinley paid close attention to the strong anti-war consensus of the business community, and strengthened his resolve to use diplomacy and negotiation rather than brute force to end the Spanish tyranny in Cuba.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A speech delivered by Republican Senator
       <a href="/wiki/Redfield_Proctor" title="Redfield Proctor">
        Redfield Proctor
       </a>
       of Vermont on March 17, 1898, thoroughly analyzed the situation and greatly strengthened the pro-war cause. Proctor concluded that war was the only answer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cubarmy_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cubarmy-71">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=1wv5KHk2_dsC&amp;pg=PA210" rel="nofollow">
          210
         </a>
        </span>
       </sup>
       Many in the business and religious communities which had until then opposed war, switched sides, leaving McKinley and Speaker Reed almost alone in their resistance to a war.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On April 11, McKinley ended his resistance and asked Congress for authority to send American troops to Cuba to end the civil war there, knowing that Congress would force a war.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_American_War_transport_Seneca.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="377" data-file-width="603" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Spanish_American_War_transport_Seneca.jpg/250px-Spanish_American_War_transport_Seneca.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Spanish_American_War_transport_Seneca.jpg/375px-Spanish_American_War_transport_Seneca.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Spanish_American_War_transport_Seneca.jpg/500px-Spanish_American_War_transport_Seneca.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_American_War_transport_Seneca.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The American transport ship
         <i>
          Seneca
         </i>
         , a chartered vessel that carried troops to Puerto Rico and Cuba
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On April 19, while Congress was considering
       <a href="/wiki/Joint_resolution" title="Joint resolution">
        joint resolutions
       </a>
       supporting Cuban independence, Republican Senator
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_M._Teller" title="Henry M. Teller">
        Henry M. Teller
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">
        Colorado
       </a>
       proposed the
       <a href="/wiki/Teller_Amendment" title="Teller Amendment">
        Teller Amendment
       </a>
       to ensure that the U.S. would not establish permanent control over Cuba after the war. The amendment, disclaiming any intention to annex Cuba, passed the Senate 42 to 35; the House concurred the same day, 311 to 6. The amended resolution demanded Spanish withdrawal and authorized the President to use as much military force as he thought necessary to help Cuba gain independence from Spain. President McKinley signed the joint resolution on April 20, 1898, and the ultimatum was sent to Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stat33.738_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-stat33.738-20">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In response, Spain severed diplomatic relations with the United States on April 21. On the same day, the U.S. Navy began a blockade of Cuba.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trask57_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-trask57-21">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spain stated, it would
       <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_war" title="Declaration of war">
        declare war
       </a>
       if the US forces invaded its territory, on April 23. On April 25, the U.S. Congress declared that a state of war between the U.S. and Spain had de facto existed since April 21, the day the blockade of Cuba had begun.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trask57_21-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-trask57-21">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_vessels.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="881" data-file-width="1990" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Spanish_vessels.jpg/220px-Spanish_vessels.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Spanish_vessels.jpg/330px-Spanish_vessels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Spanish_vessels.jpg/440px-Spanish_vessels.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_vessels.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Spanish Vessels captured up to evening of May 1, 1898
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Navy was ready, but the Army was not well-prepared for the war and made radical changes in plans and quickly purchased supplies. In the spring of 1898, the strength of the Regular U.S. Army was just 25,000 men. The Army wanted 50,000 new men but received over 220,000 through volunteers and the mobilization of
       <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" title="National Guard of the United States">
        state National Guard units
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-75">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       even gaining nearly 100,000 men on the first night after the explosion of the USS
       <i>
        Maine
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_historical_interpretations">
        Alternative historical interpretations
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Department of State of the United States of America summarizes the aftermath of the war for the Filipino people:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        After its defeat in the Spanish–American War of 1898, Spain ceded its longstanding colony of the Philippines to the United States in the Treaty of Paris. On February 4, 1899, just two days before the U.S. Senate ratified the treaty, fighting broke out between American forces and Filipino nationalists led by Emilio Aguinaldo, who sought independence rather than a change in colonial rulers. The ensuing Philippine-American War lasted three years and resulted in the death of over 4,200 American and over 20,000 Filipino combatants. As many as 200,000 Filipino civilians died from violence, famine, and disease.
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_last_stand_of_the_Spanish_Garrison.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="612" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/The_last_stand_of_the_Spanish_Garrison.jpg/220px-The_last_stand_of_the_Spanish_Garrison.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/The_last_stand_of_the_Spanish_Garrison.jpg/330px-The_last_stand_of_the_Spanish_Garrison.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/The_last_stand_of_the_Spanish_Garrison.jpg/440px-The_last_stand_of_the_Spanish_Garrison.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_last_stand_of_the_Spanish_Garrison.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The last stand of the Spanish Garrison in Cuba by
         <a href="/wiki/Murat_Halstead" title="Murat Halstead">
          Murat Halstead
         </a>
         , 1898
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1901, novelist
       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain">
        Mark Twain
       </a>
       wrote about the aftermath of the war for the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       :
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        We have robbed a trusting friend of his land and his liberty; we have invited clean young men to shoulder a discredited musket and do bandit's work under a flag which bandits have been accustomed to fear, not to follow; we have debauched America's honor and blackened her face before the world.
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       In his
       <i>
        War and Empire
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-24">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Prof. Paul Atwood of the University of Massachusetts (Boston) writes:
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        The Spanish–American War was fomented on outright lies and trumped up accusations against the intended enemy. ... War fever in the general population never reached a critical temperature until the accidental sinking of the
        <i>
         USS Maine
        </i>
        was deliberately, and falsely, attributed to Spanish villainy. ... In a cryptic message ... Senator lodge wrote that 'There may be an explosion any day in Cuba which would settle a great many things. We have got a battleship in the harbor of Havana, and our fleet, which overmatches anything the Spanish have, is masked at the Dry Tortugas.'
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       In his autobiography,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">
        Theodore Roosevelt
       </a>
       gave his views of the origins of the war:
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        Our own direct interests were great, because of the Cuban tobacco and sugar, and especially because of Cuba's relation to the projected Isthmian [Panama] Canal. But even greater were our interests from the standpoint of humanity. ... It was our duty, even more from the standpoint of National honor than from the standpoint of National interest, to stop the devastation and destruction. Because of these considerations I favored war.
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pacific_theater">
        Pacific theater
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pacifico-98.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="411" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Pacifico-98.jpg/350px-Pacifico-98.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Pacifico-98.jpg 1.5x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pacifico-98.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Pacific theatre of the Spanish–American War
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the 333 years of Spanish rule, the Philippines developed from a small overseas colony governed from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">
        Viceroyalty of New Spain
       </a>
       to a land with modern elements in the cities. The Spanish-speaking middle classes of the 19th century were mostly educated in the liberal ideas coming from Europe. Among these
       <a href="/wiki/Ilustrado" title="Ilustrado">
        Ilustrados
       </a>
       was the Filipino national hero
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal" title="José Rizal">
        José Rizal
       </a>
       , who demanded larger reforms from the Spanish authorities. This movement eventually led to the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">
        Philippine Revolution
       </a>
       against Spanish colonial rule. The revolution had been in a state of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Truce" title="Truce">
        truce
       </a>
       since the signing of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pact_of_Biak-na-Bato" title="Pact of Biak-na-Bato">
        Pact of Biak-na-Bato
       </a>
       in 1897, with revolutionary leaders having accepted exile outside of the country.
      </p>
      <p>
       On April 23, 1898, a document appeared in the
       <i>
        Manila Gazette
       </i>
       newspaper warning of the impeding war and calling for Filipinos to participate on the side of Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [e]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="570" data-file-width="740" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg/250px-USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg/375px-USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg/500px-USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Olympia_art_NH_91881-KN_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_Bay" title="Battle of Manila Bay">
          Battle of Manila Bay
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first battle between American and Spanish forces was at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_Bay_(1898)" title="Battle of Manila Bay (1898)">
        Manila Bay
       </a>
       where, on May 1,
       <a href="/wiki/Commodore_(rank)" title="Commodore (rank)">
        Commodore
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/George_Dewey" title="George Dewey">
        George Dewey
       </a>
       , commanding the U.S. Navy's
       <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_Squadron" title="Asiatic Squadron">
        Asiatic Squadron
       </a>
       aboard
       <a href="/wiki/USS_Olympia_(C-6)" title="USS Olympia (C-6)">
        USS
        <i>
         Olympia
        </i>
       </a>
       , in a matter of hours defeated a Spanish squadron under Admiral
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patricio_Montojo" title="Patricio Montojo">
        Patricio Montojo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [f]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dewey managed this with only nine wounded.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With the German seizure of
       <a href="/wiki/Qingdao" title="Qingdao">
        Tsingtao
       </a>
       in 1897, Dewey's squadron had become the only naval force in the Far East without a local base of its own, and was beset with coal and ammunition problems.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHRJune1988p659_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AHRJune1988p659-90">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite these problems, the Asiatic Squadron not only destroyed the Spanish fleet but also captured the harbor of Manila.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHRJune1988p659_90-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AHRJune1988p659-90">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following Dewey's victory, Manila Bay was filled with the warships of Britain, Germany, France, and Japan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHRJune1988p659_90-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-AHRJune1988p659-90">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The German fleet of eight ships, ostensibly in Philippine waters to protect German interests, acted provocatively – cutting in front of American ships, refusing to salute the United States flag (according to customs of naval courtesy), taking soundings of the harbor, and landing supplies for the besieged Spanish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Germans, with interests of their own, were eager to take advantage of whatever opportunities the conflict in the islands might afford.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dolan1991_93-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dolan1991-93">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was a fear at the time that the islands would become a German possession.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Americans called the bluff of the Germans, threatening conflict if the aggression continued, and the Germans backed down.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dolan1991_93-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dolan1991-93">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the time, the Germans expected the confrontation in the Philippines to end in an American defeat, with the revolutionaries capturing Manila and leaving the Philippines ripe for German picking.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Commodore Dewey transported
       <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Aguinaldo" title="Emilio Aguinaldo">
        Emilio Aguinaldo
       </a>
       , a Filipino leader who had led rebellion against Spanish rule in the Philippines in 1896, from exile in Hong Kong to the Philippines to rally more Filipinos against the Spanish colonial government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Library_of_Congress_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-U.S._Library_of_Congress-97">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By June 9, Aguinaldo's forces controlled the provinces of
       <a href="/wiki/Bulacan" title="Bulacan">
        Bulacan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cavite" title="Cavite">
        Cavite
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Laguna_(province)" title="Laguna (province)">
        Laguna
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Batangas" title="Batangas">
        Batangas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bataan" title="Bataan">
        Bataan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zambales" title="Zambales">
        Zambales
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pampanga" title="Pampanga">
        Pampanga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pangasinan" title="Pangasinan">
        Pangasinan
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mindoro" title="Mindoro">
        Mindoro
       </a>
       , and had laid siege to Manila.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On June 12, Aguinaldo proclaimed the independence of the Philippines.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pinas_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pinas-100">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On August 5, on instructions from Spain, Governor General Basilo Augistin turned over command of the Philippines to his deputy, Fermin Jaudenes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On August 13, with American commanders unaware that a cease-fire had been signed between Spain and the U.S. on the previous day in Washington D.C., American forces captured the city of Manila from the Spanish in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1898)" title="Battle of Manila (1898)">
        Battle of Manila
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Library_of_Congress_97-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-U.S._Library_of_Congress-97">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This battle marked the end of Filipino–American collaboration, as the American action of preventing Filipino forces from entering the captured city of Manila was deeply resented by the Filipinos. This later led to the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">
        Philippine–American War
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lac126_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lac126-103">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which would prove to be more deadly and costly than the Spanish–American War.
      </p>
      <p>
       The U.S. had sent a force of some 11,000 ground troops to the Philippines. On August 14, 1899, Spanish Captain-General Jaudenes formally capitulated and U.S. Generally Merritt formally accepted the surrender and declared the establishment of a U.S. military government in occupation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       That same day, the
       <a href="/wiki/Schurman_Commission" title="Schurman Commission">
        Schurman Commission
       </a>
       recommended that the U.S. retain control of the Philippines, possibly granting independence in the future.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On December 10, 1898, the Spanish government ceded the Philippines to the United States in the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">
        Treaty of Paris
       </a>
       . Armed conflict broke out between U.S. forces and the Filipinos when U.S. troops began to take the place of the Spanish in control of the country after the end of the war, resulting in the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">
        Philippine–American War
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Guam">
        Guam
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
